arXiv:2305.09851v1  [math.FA]  16 May 2023Convergence of commutator of linear integral
operators with separable kernel representing
monomial covariance type commutation
relations in /u1D473/u1D491
Domingos Djinja, Sergei Silvestrov, and Alex Behakanira Tu mwesigye
Abstract Representations by linear integral operators on /u1D43F/u1D45Dspaces over measure
spaces are investigated for the polynomial covariance type commutation relations
and more general two-sided generalizations of covariance c ommutation relations
extending simultaneously the covariance and the reciproca l covariance type com-
mutation relations. Necessary and suﬃcient conditions for the deﬁning kernels of
the integral operators are obtained for the operators to sat isfy such commutation
relations associated to pairs of polynomials. Representat ions by integral operators
are studied both for general polynomial covariance type com mutation relations and
for important classes of polynomial covariance commutatio n relations associated
with arbitrary monomials and aﬃne functions. The convergen ce of commutators of
operators in the sequences of non-commuting operators sati sfying the correspond-
ing monomial covariance commutation relation is investiga ted, and the sequences of
such non-commuting operators converging to commuting oper ators, are presented.
Key words: integral operators, covariance commutation relations, co mmutator
MSC 2020: 47A62, 47G10, 47L80, 47L65

1 Introduction
Commutation relations of the form
/u1D434/u1D435=/u1D435/u1D439(/u1D434) (1)
where/u1D434,/u1D435are elements of an associative algebra and /u1D439is function of the elements
of the algebra, are important in many areas of Mathematics an d applications. Such
commutation relations are usually called covariance relat ions, crossed product rela-
tions or semi-direct product relations. A pair of elements o f an algebra that satisfy
(1) is called a representation of this relation [46].
Representations of covariance commutation relations (1) b y linear operators are
important for study of actions and induced representations of groups and semigroups,
crossed product operator algebras, dynamical systems, har monic analysis, wavelets
and fractal analysis and, hence have applications in physic s and engineering [4, 5,
21–23,30–32,38,39,46].
A description of the structure of representations for the re lation (1) and more
general families of self-adjoint operators satisfying suc h relations by bounded and
unbounded self-adjoint linear operators on a Hilbert space use reordering formulas
for functions of the algebra elements and operators satisfy ing covariance commuta-
tion relation, functional calculus and spectral represent ation of operators and inter-
play with dynamical systems generated by iteration of invol ved in the commutation
relations maps is presented in [3,7–9,14–18,24,25,33–38, 40–44,46–60].
Constructions of representations of polynomial covarianc e commutations rela-
tions by pairs of linear integral operators with general ker nels, linear integral opera-
tors with separable kernels and linear multiplication oper ator have been considered
in [11–13].
In this paper, we construct representations of the covarian ce type commutation re-
lations (1) and more general relation /u1D43B(/u1D434)/u1D435=/u1D435/u1D439(/u1D434), where/u1D439,/u1D43Bare polynomials,
by pairs of linear integral operators with separable kernel s on Banach spaces /u1D43F/u1D45Dover
measure spaces. These results generalize results in [12] an d gives also results for the
reciprocal commutation relation /u1D435/u1D434=/u1D439(/u1D434)/u1D435of (1). We consider representations
of commutation relations /u1D43B(/u1D434)/u1D435=/u1D435/u1D439(/u1D434)by linear integral operators deﬁned by
kernels satisfying diﬀerent conditions and derive conditi ons on such kernel functions
so that the corresponding operators satisfy /u1D43B(/u1D434)/u1D435=/u1D435/u1D439(/u1D434)for polynomials /u1D439,/u1D43B.
Representation by integral operators are studied both for g eneral polynomial co-
variance commutation relations and for important classes o f polynomial covariance
commutation relations associated to arbitrary monomials a nd to aﬃne functions.
Examples of integral operators with separable kernels on /u1D43F/u1D45Dspaces representing the
relation/u1D434/u1D435=/u1D6FF/u1D435/u1D4342,/u1D6FF∈R\{0}are constructed in [12]. Furthermore, in this paper,
convergence of commutators of those sequences of non-commu ting operators which
satisfy the correspondingmonomial covariance commutatio nrelation is investigated.
This paper is organized in four sections. After the introduc tion, we present in
Section 2 some preliminaries, notations, basic deﬁnitions and a useful lemma. In
Section 3, we present representations when both /u1D434and/u1D435are linear integral ope-Convergence of commutator of linear integral operators wit h separable 3
rators with separable kernels acting on the Banach spaces /u1D43F/u1D45D. In Section 4 we
present sequences of non-commuting operators which satisf y monomial covariance
commutation relation and converge to commuting operators.

4 Sequences of non commuting operators that converge to
commuting operator
In this section we construct families of non-commuting oper ators{/u1D436/u1D45A}or{/u1D437/u1D45A}
such that satisfy the commutation relation /u1D436/u1D437=/u1D6FF/u1D437/u1D4362and converge in norm to
an operator /u1D436or/u1D437(/bardbl/u1D436/u1D45A−/u1D436/bardbl/u1D438→0 or/bardbl/u1D437/u1D45A−/u1D437/bardbl/u1D438→0,/u1D45A→ ∞ ), respectively,
such that /u1D436and/u1D437commute. We ﬁrst present two lemmas which relate conditions
of commutativity and convergence of sequence of operators. We assume that the
reader is familiar with deﬁnitions of convergence of operat or sequences and norm
properties. For further reading about the norm deﬁnition, u niform convergence of
operators and their basic properties, please read [6,19,27 ,28].
Lemma 2. Let/u1D438be a normed vector space. Let /u1D436/u1D45A:/u1D438→/u1D438for each positive integer
be a bounded linear operators and let /u1D437:/u1D438→/u1D438be a bounded linear operator.
Suppose that the sequence {/u1D436/u1D45A}converge in norm to an operator /u1D436. Then, the
sequence {/u1D436/u1D45A/u1D437−/u1D437/u1D436/u1D45A}converge in norm to zero if and only if /u1D436/u1D437=/u1D437/u1D436.
Proof. Necessity (only if): Suppose that the sequence of bounded li near operators
{/u1D436/u1D45A/u1D437−/u1D437/u1D436/u1D45A}converge in norm to zero. Then, by applying linearity and nor mConvergence of commutator of linear integral operators wit h separable 13
properties, we have, for each positive integer /u1D45A, the following:

=/bardbl(/u1D436−/u1D436/u1D45A)/u1D437+/u1D436/u1D45A/u1D437−/u1D437/u1D436/u1D45A+/u1D437(/u1D436/u1D45A−/u1D436)/bardbl/u1D438
≤2/bardbl/u1D436−/u1D436/u1D45A/bardbl/u1D438·/bardbl/u1D437/bardbl/u1D438+/bardbl/u1D436/u1D45A/u1D437−/u1D437/u1D436/u1D45A/bardbl/u1D438.
Therefore,

Remark 6. In connections to Theorems 2–9 , if /u1D7060∈Λthen the commutator [/u1D434,/u1D435]=
/u1D434/u1D435−/u1D435/u1D434exists for parameters at point /u1D7060∈Λand it is equal zero under some
convergenceconditions, however there are issues regardin g convergenceof operators
/u1D434and/u1D435. If/u1D7060∈cl(Λ)\Λthen[/u1D434,/u1D435]=/u1D434/u1D435−/u1D435/u1D434, operators /u1D434,/u1D435might not exist for
parameters at point /u1D7060. However the commutator [/u1D434,/u1D435]=/u1D434/u1D435−/u1D435/u1D434and operators
/u1D434,/u1D435exist for parameters in Λand when moving these parameters in these set to
a point/u1D7060∈cl(Λ)\Λ, the commutator [/u1D434,/u1D435]=/u1D434/u1D435−/u1D435/u1D434converges to zero under
some conditions.
